Post_ID: 2761202702763851797 | Post_Code: CZRwzqLFoAV | Likes: 123 | Time Stamp: 1643381034 | Tags: [] | Caption: Leave No Trace Principle 2: Travel and Camp on Durable Surfaces â¬‡ï¸<\br><\br>Continuing with our LNT series, letâ€™s talk about principle 2!<\br><\br>Choosing durable surfaces to travel and camp on greatly impacts the degradation of the environment. <\br><\br>ğŸ¥¾RULE OF THUMB: stay on the provided trails. Trails are built to be able to limit the destruction of the nearby areas, to keep the traffic in a designated area. So, whenever possible, stay on the trail.<\br><\br>ğŸ¥¾BUT, LETâ€™S BE REAL, there are times we have all gone off the trail! Whether youâ€™re searching for a private â€œbathroomâ€ area, taking a lunch break,  finding a campsite, or scrambling up some rock to get to a vista, itâ€™s just part of hiking! <\br><\br>ğŸª¨ Because of this, itâ€™s important to BE CONSCIOUS of where you travel off trail. Rocky areas are often able to withstand a lot more travel than vegetation and living soil. <\br><\br>ğŸ‘£ If you must travel through these areas, be conscious of your impact. (Sometimes this means spreading out from your group (vegetation), sometimes it means following exact footprints (soil))<\br><\br>ğŸ•CAMPING on durable surfaces:<\br>Choose a campsite that either already has very high traffic (no vegetation left) or, in less trafficked areas, find locations you can have the least impact on. Generally, rock and sand are great areas to set up camp, as they will be able to withstand campers. <\br><\br>â›ºï¸ğŸ¥˜CAMP COOKING: Set up camp kitchens on Rocky areas to avoid constant trampling on vegetation and soil. <\br><\br>This principle is EXTENSIVE and every situation differs. Your situation changes in different locations, the type of trip, and the local environment. We highly recommend you go check out lnt.org for more information on how to implement this principle, but we hope this gave you a good idea of the general guidelines!<\br><\br>Overall, it is our jobs to take into consideration the environment around us to decide how we can best limit our impact on each trip.<\br><\br>We also feel itâ€™s important to recognize that while â€œstay on the trailâ€ is a good rule of thumb, there are circumstances when you just CANâ€™T. Being able to know how to handle those moments and travel off trail responsibly is super important and can help us all to take better care of these lands!

Post_ID: 2759941819536871849 | Post_Code: CZNSHZKPZGp | Likes: 24 | Time Stamp: 1643230725 | Tags: ['#WildernessWednesday', '#willdernessvolunteers', '#givingsomethingback', '#wildernesswednesdays', '#sangoroniowilderness', '#sangorgonio', '#sangorgoniopeak', '#sangorgoniopass', '#usfs', '#sanbernardinonationalforest', '#itsallyours', '#usforestservice', '#designatedwilderness', '#pacificcresttrail', '#pct', '#bureauoflandmanagement', '#blm', '#california', '#oldgraybackmountain', '#oldgrayback', '#optoutside', '#leavenotrace', '#lnt', '#photography', '#wilderness', '#camping', '#backpacking', '#colorpalette', '#colors', '#colorwheel'] | Caption: Happy #WildernessWednesday! Today we're taking in the beauty found in the San Gorgonio Wilderness in Southern California! Nestled in San Bernardino National Forest, this designated wilderness also resides within the Sand to Snow National Monument. <\br>.<\br>The San Gorgonio Wilderness consists of sub-alpine landscape surrounded by desert to the east, and covers 94,000+ acres. With elevations from 4,400'-11,500', you can experience soft rolling foothills, to canyons, to steep, impressive mountains. Due to the elevation gradient, this wilderness has a transition between desert, coastal and mountain environments, including the different types of vegetation representative of each elevation.<\br>.<\br>The U.S. Congress designated the San Gorgonio Wilderness in 1964, making it one of the first designated wilderness areas in the U.S. The wilderness is named after San Gorgonio Mountain, which at 11,499 ft. is the highest peak in California south of the Sierra Nevada. San Gorgonio Mountain, however, was originally known as "Old Grayback" by locals until officially designated by the US Geological Survey in 1899.<\br>.<\br>There are 81 miles of trails in the National Forest section of the Wilderness, and ~20 miles of the Pacific Crest National Scenic Trail in the Bureau of Land Management portion. <\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>#willdernessvolunteers #givingsomethingback #wildernesswednesdays  #sangoroniowilderness #sangorgonio #sangorgoniopeak #sangorgoniopass #usfs #sanbernardinonationalforest #itsallyours #usforestservice #designatedwilderness #pacificcresttrail #pct #bureauoflandmanagement #blm #california #oldgraybackmountain #oldgrayback #optoutside #leavenotrace #lnt #photography #wilderness #camping #backpacking #colorpalette #colors #colorwheel

Sorghum syrup is similar to maple syrup or molasses, a sweet, sticky concoction derived form the sorghum plant. To make sorghum syrup, you crush the stalks of the sorghum plant, which produces a juice. The juice is then boiled, so that excess water evaporates as steam and only the sweet syrup remains.<\br>The Lyon family enslaved people prior to the Civil War, and continued to live on and farm the Lyon property until the early 2000's. This mill was used by later generations of the Lyon family as they worked on the farm. You can experience the full tour of the Flat Rock Archives by signing up for an @airbnb experience, where Johnny Waits leads you on a tour through Flat Rock's history, from enslavement to the present day.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>.<\br>#ArabiaMountainNationalHeritageArea #ArabiaMountain #PanolaMountain #NationalHeritageArea#NationalPark #NationalHistoricSite #StatePark #GAStateParks #GeorgiaStatePark #Parks #Hiking #HikeLife #WanderNorthGA #AtlantaTrails #RespectThePark #LeaveNoTrace #OptOutside #RecreateResponsibly #LNT #history #blackhistory #sorghum
